              # to.dummy(ext$CHR, "RefGene"),
               to.dummy(ext$Relation_to_UCSC_CpG_Island, "RefGene"),

# with external data
temp <- c()
  
for (i in 1:20) {
  
  cv_xrnet <- tune_xrnet(
    x = x.train,
    y = y.train,
    external = RefGeneGroup,
    family = "gaussian",
    control = xrnet.control(tolerance = 1e-6)
  )
  
  y_pre <- predict(cv_xrnet, newdata = x.test, type = "response")
  if(i == 1){
    temp[i] = mean((y.test - y_pre) ^ 2)
  }else{
    temp[i] = temp[i-1] + mean((y.test - y_pre) ^ 2)
  }
}
temp

Here’s another analysis you might try to do for Friday.

Get the list of features that are in the prediction model from the paper. Then save the annotation information for those features and let’s analyze them. Do you have enhancers in that a list? Are there more enhancers than expected by chance? (Chi-square test for a 2x2 table. Enhancer yes/no vs feature in prediction model yes/no. What about features in TSS200? Are any features in the list in TSS200?

Create 2 variables: feature is in the prediction model from the paper we read (yes/no). Feature is in an enhancer (Yes=TRUE/No=blank).

Now create a 2x2 table and compute a chi-square test to compare proportions. Proportion of features in prediction model that are in an enhancer vs proportion of features that were not in the model that are in an enhancer (reference group).
